text:
Trust me, you will not miss the meat in this sandwich!  I also broiled my veggies because of the snow outside on top of the grill.  The only veggie I added was green pepper only because I had one.  I will use a large red onion next time because we love the carmelized flavor of the onion under the broiler. I also sprayed my veggies with balsamic vinegar for some extra "zip". Served the veggies on hearty multi-grain rolls from Whole Foods - - use the best bread possible because it truly will make or break the sandwich.  Excellent recipe, Heather!!

text:
This was quite possibly the best sandwich I've ever had (my hubby said the same thing).  We put it in italian-seasoned focaccia and after the veggies were done (we grilled them on a gas grill), we assembled the sandwich and wrapped in foil and put in a 350F oven for 20 minutes.  Incredible.  I want another one already.  For us, this made 2 very large sandwiches.  UPDATE: we've made these about once every other week and we still haven't gotten sick of them.  Make sure and make the sauce about ahead of time and let it sit for about an hour in the fridge to mix the flavors well.

text:
Wow, now this is veggie heaven! What a fabulous sandwich that's not only bursting with vibrant colors but it's also bursting with a lot of flavor! Grilling the veggies really gives it a nice smoky quality that tastes great. I added a bit of garlic, rosemary, thyme, fresh lemon juice, kosher salt, and cracked black pepper to the olive oil to baste the veggies while grilling. I also grilled some thick sliced tomato along with the other veggies and opted for some mild cheddar cheese vs. feta. This was great on focaccia and I'd love to experiment with other types of bread - this recipe is a definite keeper!

text:
This was really good.  I had some doubts, even after reading all of the other positive reviews, because I didn't know how well my meat-eating, preponderantly male family would take to an all-veggie sandwich.  They loved it - and so did I.  I only had minced garlic, so I roasted some of that in a glass dish in my toaster oven for the aioli.  I used sliced red and green bell peppers, zucchini, fresh sliced mushroom, tomatoes and carmelized onions for my vegetables.  I didn't have rosemary, so I just used dried basil and parsley instead.  I used Monterey Jack cheese and used English muffins as my base - yum!  I'll definitely, definitely be making these again.  Thank you for the recipe!

text:
I baked, "Michael's Foccacia Bread," from this website, which is VERY good by the way. To begin with I made the dressing and marianted for an hour to let the ingredients marry. I sliced the red bell peppers and red onions into ringlets. I sliced the zucchini and yellow squash, lengthwise, in strips, from the top down. I brushed oil on each vegetable and placed it on the grill to cook. Within 3 minutes I had nice dark grill marks on the vegetables and they appeared to get soft so I flipped it over to cook the other side. I placed the bottom half of the bread onto the grill to heat it up. I did the same with the top half only I placed it cutside down first to get it heated and toasted up nicely. I spread a little of the dressing onto the bread, sprinkled it with the feta cheese and layered the vegetables on each sandwich. The ingredients, vegetables and the dressing amount is enough to fill exactly four "good size" foccacia sandwiches. This is absolutely delicious! The dressing is just perfect. The lemon juice and garlic work well in the mayonnaise-nothing is too "tangy" or "oily". The foccacia bread tastes great because it is freshly baked, tasty and has fresh herbs baked right into it! With all the grilled vegetables layered on this, I feel good knowing I ate healthy. The vegetables are only seasoned with olive oil, nothing more, and tastes sweet. This is a very satisfying, healthy and fulfilling meal. Even the meat lover's in my family didn't miss the meat. Love it!

This deserves 5 stars because of its potential.  The meal was delicious, even the carnivores loved it.  I will make a few changes in the future though... Instead of toasting the bread on the grill with the cheese side up, I will put it under the broiler so the cheese side is grilled instead.  The sandwich was so crunchy that when you bight down, the filling falls out.  Portobello mushrooms are a must and I recommend marinating the vegetables in a red wine vinegar in advance.  Overall- wonderful and I can see this being a staple in my weekly meals.  Thank you!

text:
So good! The first time I made it I had used goat cheese. Mistake. The other times, I used grated parmesan cheese. Yum. Also used Costco's ciabatta rolls. Poured some oil on cookie sheet, spread thin with a paper towel. Put the veges on pan. Put a thin layer of a balsamic glaze (Costco online) on veges. Broiled on second level from top, about 5 min. Flipped, added another thin layer of balsamic glaze. Baked another 5 min. FYI- I put the onion on a separate cookie sheet and broiled first; then took it out and put the vege cookie sheet in it's place; at the same time I then put the onion cookie sheet back in the oven, but on the rack below the veges.  (To keep warm and cook a little more.)

Please make these. You will not regret it! Not only are they so delicious, but they make for such a colorful, gorgeous meal. THE quintessential summer recipe! I grilled all the above veggies also adding tomato and basted with a mixture of olive oil, balsamic vinegar, s&p, thyme, rosemary, and garlic as others suggested (DO this! Gives the veggies awesome flavor). I used tomato basil foccacia and after spreading with the mayo and sprinkling w/ feta, I put the foccacia slices on the grill for several minutes then piled the veggies over the top and served open faced w/ my roasted corn salad on the side. WOW! So, so good and such presentation for company! Thanks for this recipe...My family will be making these ALOT during the summer! :)

text:
Allrecipes' Focaccia Bread: Do not buy bread when you can MAKE it!! this is awesome!!

Marinate the veggies for 24-48 hours in the following dressing, you will thank your self as your tummy gets fuller:)
Chop all veggies and place in a sealable container or bag.
1/4 cup balsamic vinegar
1 teaspoon garlic powder
1/4 teaspoon salt
2 TBSP Balsamic Vinegarette
stir together and pour over sliced veggies, shake to coat evenly then refrigerate, shake every few hours to keep the sauce distributed evenly, Broil and serve on homemade facaccia bread.

I have made this recipe as written (and not) many, many times and you can not go wrong with it as long as you use good quality bread.  This makes the sandwich so versatile! I like to switch out the breads and veggies based on what I have.  Today I used a round Italian Bread fresh from the bakery and left out the yellow squash, but added mushrooms instead.  Also, I prefer goat cheese in place of the feta, but that is my personal preference.  For the mayo mix, I always add a bit of capers and their juice for an extra bit of flavor.  Also, I just roast my veggies in the oven. One of my favorite sandwiches!

text:
This recipe is fantastic! Simple, versatile, and satisfying. Stubbornly carnivorous husband said he didn't even miss the meat! I made my own focaccia bread for the sandwiches- the "Focaccia Bread I" recipe from this site worked well- and shaped the loaf a little thicker than the recipe recommended for easy horizontal slicing. We substituted baby portabella mushroom slices for the yellow squash and used a vidalia onion instead of a red onion. The garlic-mayo sauce had enough "kick" on its own and was balanced nicely by the sweet/mellow flavors of the veggies we used.  One thing that made cooking this recipe a lot easier was a grill skillet (looks like a regular skillet with holes... works sort of like a grill basket but sliced veggies won't fall through). Served the dish with baked sweet potato fries tossed with olive oil, garlic, rosemary, and kosher salt, and the combination was to die for! I'm sure we'll make this recipe over and over this summer, with whatever produce happens to be in season and available at our farmers market! Delicious!

text:
This is my first review.  I made this for my son & wife as they are vegetarians..(saved a little for myself to try).  It was outstanding!!!  I used 1 each..zucchini,yellow squash,sweet onion,,red & yellow pepper & tray of steak mushrooms. Put the veggies in 1 gal zip lock bag with olive oil, balsamic vinegar and 1 1/2 tsp season salt. Shook and turned bag a few times while grill heated.  Doubled the lemon mayo but used just 1 tsp crushed fresh garlic...now am thinking 1/2tsp more might be even better and the key is to make ahead.. 4 hrs minimum so flavors can "meld". Grilled vegggies on gas grill using grill wok pan with holes...works slick.  Put on fresh baked ciabata rolls with the lemon mayo and feta..  I am not a vegetarian..but I ate 3 for my supper as it wsas delicious (and the rolls were small..that's my excuse and I am sticking to it.)  Haven't heard from the kids yet..but bet they loved it too!!  Thanks so much for the outstanding recipe!! Will make often!!!

text:
WOW. This sandwich was stupendous!  I loved everything about it!  The only things I would do differently would be to use only a little amount of feta if serving this to kids, and next time I think I will try grilling portabella mushrooms with it, I think that would make it a little more meaty since I am not a vegetarian.  Also the recipe says to eat it as an open faced sandwich.  Don't do that. Cut it in half from the side, and then cut it into fourths.  So you will have 4 sandwiches.  Get a little  mayo and feta on each piece, and after all the grilling everyone can add their own veggies.

This was excellent! I was looking for something meatless for tonight and this is what I happened upon, and am so glad to have found it! Thank you Heather!  My changes: I used generous slices of a hearty whole grain bread; added tomatoes and basil to the veggie mix and marinated in olive oil and balsamic vinegar for about 30 minutes, then baked veggies in a 400 degree oven for about 20 minutes. text:
I recently became a vegetarian, trying to transition to veganism... and this sandwich was the best sandwich I've EVER had, meat or not! Even non-veggies will LOVE it!
I added portobello as some others suggested, because I love them and they are "meaty". I also drizzled brown sugar & balsamic vinegar over the red onions while my husband was grilling. We did not have focaccia on hand or at the store, so we got hoagies, and I made a rosemary-thyme-basil-and-olive-oil mix and brushed it onto them, then popped them in the oven at 250 for 12-13 mins. I also used Nasoya "mayo" because I try to limit my egg and dairy intake as much as possible. I wrapped the assembled sandwiches in foil as another suggested and put them in also, at 300 for 6-7 mins. It was enough for 4 sandwiches.
They were SO AWESOME, if and when I go vegan, I will have to find some kind of feta approximation! WOW!!!

We have been making this sandwich so many times since we found the recipe 4 years ago on Allrecipe.com.  One time, we couldn't find focaccia bread in our local supermarket and tried it with ciabatta bread.  Since then, we always use ciabatta bread because the texture is so much better than focaccia bread.  It's crunchier and chewy and perfect match with soft sweet roasted vegetable.   We tried with Italian bread, French Baguette, sour dough bread, etc.  But we like the ciabatta bread the most.

city:

region:

text:
Here are my tips: Slice the Foccacia in two, split it so as to make an actual sandwich. Not open faced as the recipe calls for. Feta is nice but it wont melt. I marinated sliced goat cheese in a seasoned oil mixture for several hours. Basically, put herbs in some olive oil and place the cheese in. The cheese will take on more flavour. Then use this flavourful oil to brush your veg on the grill. Dont marinate the vegetables like some have suggested. In vinegar? Why would you do that to a vegetable! :-)Keep their own lovely flavour please. The raw garlic could be very strong indeed. I suggest roasting the garlic or using powder / dry garlic flakes. I suggest serving with toasted walnuts for crunch and peppery rocket/arugula/rucola leaves for a zip of flavour. Using a portobello mushroom is a great idea but it makes this a veggie burger type recipe and moves it away from its fresh veggie recipe. Eggplant/aubergine I suggest slicing and grilling as this compliments very well.Also, so that it all comes together I suggest wrapping in aluminium/tin foil for a minute or two on the grill. That way everything is hot, the cheese has a chance to melt and your bread wont blacken.

text:
My brother and I are both teens, we made this together one day for lunch for us and our parents. It took us about 35 minutes start to finish and it was DELISH! we made some changes, like shallots instead of onion (which makes it so sweet and so good!), and asparagus instead of squash (grilled asparagus is to DIE for). Really, you can do any good 4-5 vegetable combo with this sandwich and it will still melt in your mouth and warm your belly. We also used ciabatta bread instead of the focaccia but any good italian bread grilled up with that yummy mayo-oil-lemon glaze and melted feta will be so great. Such a crowd-pleaser good for any summer occasion! MUST TRY!

text:
I liked this sandwich. Thank you for sharing. My husband, on the other hand, did not like the sandwich - he loved the veges, but he felt the spread was too garlicky and wasn't a fan of the feta. Changes I made: I did not grill the veges. I roasted them in the oven. I cut up all the veges and put them on a foil lined baking sheet. I salted and peppered them and tossed them in 2 tablespoons of olive oil with a pinch of sugar.  I roasted them in a 450 degree oven for about 25 mins.  I used a Tuscan Garlic loaf I purchased from the bakery at my local grocery store. Otherwise I made it as stated and kept it as an open face sandwich.

text:
This recipe was really good but I experienced two issues in its preparation.  First, no one in my family likes mayo so I had to come up with a replacement.  I used a mixture of cream cheese and lowfat plain yogurt.  Very good!  Second, enough veggies to make these sandwiches takes up a LOT of space on your grill resulting in difficulty turning all of them.  If you don't have a veggie griller basket, I recommend heeding others' advice and broiling your veggies in your oven.  Overall, the recipe was delicious and my family is still talking about it!  Enjoy!

text:
So easy and quick and pleases everyone I've served it to!  I've served this twice now and we absolutely love it.  I have a stovetop grill pan that will make those gorgeous grill marks on the veggies, so I've made the sandwich on both an outside grill and inside as well ... this sandwich turned out just fine either way.

This last time I made some minor adjustments for personal tastes, but if you follow this recipe to the letter you won't be disappointed.  I chopped up some fresh flatleaf parsley to go into the mayo mix and used a bit more garlic.  We love feta cheese so I didn't bother measuring, just crumbled it on top of the bread.  I didn't have a red onion this last time and used a sweet one ... perfection!  This sandwich is VERY forgiving to a few changes.  I also slipped a few fresh tomato slices into the finished product just before serving - the last time I just sliced them up and served them on the side.  

This recipe won't disappoint, give it a shot!

text:
This is a delicious recipe!  I was too lazy to start up the grill when I made this recipe, so I broiled my veggies in foil tents instead.  I added some liquid smoke, and they turned out great!  I noticed some confusion in the other comments about the focaccia bread.  This is a very thin type of bread, and when used for sandwiches it is cut horizontally to make two even thinner slices of bread.  Also, this recipe calls for "open face" sandwiches, meaning there is not a slice of bread on top.  That is how 4 servings can be made out of 2 pieces of bread, which are each cut in half.

Wonderful! I added a little salt to the garlic mayo, and let it sit for a few hours in the fridge before making the sandwich. I will definitely make these again.

text:
This was REALLY delicious!  As others suggested, I marinated the veggies beforehand and I think that turned out to be a smart move.  I bought 1 zucchini, 1 yellow squash, about half of a sweet red pepper and about 8 stalks of asparagus.  I tossed them with 3 tbsp oil, 1 tbsp soy sauce, 1 tbsp balsamic vinegar, 1/4 tsp salt, 1/4 tsp pepper.  I marinated them in the fridge for about 45 minutes, stirring them occasionally.  Because it's a bit cold here today, I roasted the vegetables instead of grilling them: about 20 minutes at 450deg (stirring halfway).  I then put the sauce on the rolls, then some shredded mozzarella and shredded parmesan, and put them under the broiler for a minute or two.  The sauce with the marinade was really quite delicious.  I will cut back on the oil next time because 3 tbsp was a bit too much for that amount of vegetables.  I can't wait to try this again!

text:
This recipe is delicious! I used a vegetable grill pan to grill the veggies- added  grape tomatoes and 8 oz. sliced portabella mushrooms to the mixture, and added a few splashes of balsamic vinegar to the olive oil, salt, pepper and basil, and marinated the veggies while the coals were heating up. I used a loaf of French bread. I also used Monterey Jack and sharp cheddar cheese in place of feta. I used garlic powder because I was lazy and didn't feel like peeling and chopping garlic cloves- I added maybe between 1/2 tsp- 1 tsp. garlic powder to the mayonnaise and lemon juice. I will make this again. Made 4 very large open face sandwiches. I wrapped the 2 remaining sandwiches in foil and plan on reheating in the oven at 400 degrees for 20-25 minutes later this week. update: the plan to eat these later this week- lasted all of 3 hours after dinner. I preheated the oven to 425 and heated the foil wrapped sandwich for 20 minutes. Crispy, hot and delicious! Several days later- still crispy, hot and delicious after being wrapped in foil and refrigerated for 3 days, then baked as above. The vegetables are a little softer than the original just grilled sandwich, but still delicious!

text:
I made this using the focaccia bread recipe on this web site. I rolled the focaccia bread thin so I didn't need to horizontally slice the bread in half. I doubled the ingredients for this recipe. Also, I didn't have an outside grill so I baked the vegetables at 450 F and turned the temperature up to 500 F for the last 5 minutes.  I cut the focaccia bread into slices and then flipped the cheese side of the bread over, placed the mayo mixture, feta cheese and vegetables on the slices and baked it at 450 for about 5 minutes. This came out great and I will definitely make it again.

OK, this recipe is fantastic! I changed just a few things. I added white mushrooms and omitted the squash. I also halved the garlic after reading the reviews, which I recommend. text:
Such a simple and delicious sandwich to make! Even my carnivorous husband loved this veggie sandwich! The mayo mixture really adds a lovely flavor. There is a strong flavor of garlic, but if you love garlic like we do, it will be fine. You can easily reduce the amount of garlic to 1.5-2 cloves so that it's not overpowering for you. Since we don't care for feta cheese, I used provolone. I've made this twice since the weekend and added sauteed portobello mushroom slices (sauteed in evoo, salt/pepper, and a little balsamic vinegar). This recipe is very versatile in that you could probably add other grilled or roasted veggies. Overall, there is no need to adjust the measurements to the recipe. It's perfect as written!

SO DELICIOUS! Made this for dinner last night and I am making it again tonight. As someone who is actively seeking health-conscious vegetarian options, I really gravitated toward this recipe. Glad I did! Only changes I made: I used Olive Oil/Balsamic Vinaigrette on the veggies, I used a nice piece of italian bread toasted in the oven, I omitted the cheese (IT DOES NOT NEED IT!) text:
This is a very good sandwich. Per a very rainy day, we had to roast the veges in the oven at 400.  We did not have a red bell but used the green one we had on hand with great results and added some sliced portabellas which we roasted along with all the other veges. As only feeding 2, used one focaccia, but did not cut the mayo mix - thank goodness, as it was barely enough for a light coating on the 2 halves.  After putting all veges and the cheese on the bread halves, wrapped in foil, placed cast iron pot on top and placed in oven at 400 to cook like an oven baked panini.  We could not eat the whole thing - even cutting in half, it was enough for four.  Thanks for sharing this easy, yummy recipe.

I have found recipes on here that have rave reviews before & when I try them, I'm not that impressed. I kind of thought that was going to happen here, but this really is a fantastic recipe. text:
It was delicious and filling!I made a couple minor changes-  I added sun dried tomato pesto to the mayonaise spread because I had it on hand, it adds some complexity to the sauce and tastes great mixed with the lemon. (about 1 heaping tablespoon)  After I chopped up the veggies I added a splash of  balsalmic vinegar and pepper, and then refrigerated for an hour. I used french rolls because I couldn't find focaccia bread- they were still delicious.  Also, I don't have a grill so I just cooked the veggies at 350 for 15 minutes, then broiled for the last 5 minutes with the bread and cheese also, which gave it a great crunch. Yum.   I didn't add any additional veggies (some add potobella mushrooms but I don't care for them) but I wish I had grilled more because this is a great dish and could eat it over and over again. You seriously won't miss the meat, and it gives you a great 'full' feeling without any heavyness.

text:
Oh, yes! This was fabulous! My teen daughter is a die-hard vegetarian and I'm a semi-veggie so we're always looking for something new and tasty. This recipe did not disappoint. I used the Foreman Grill and splashed some raspberry vinagrette on the veggies in addition to a swipe of olive oil. It took about 15 minutes for the veggies to get crisp/soft. My garlic was dry & husk-ey, so I used garlic powder and subbed light mayo. Tasted great anyway! I also used way more veggies than the recipe called for including some small portabello mushrooms. Instead of Focaccia bread, I used french bread. I also used a slice of 2% swiss which was yummy. After I made the sandwiches, I threw some frozen chicken tenders on for my son and served it on a toasted bun along with the rest of the mayo dressing - he announced it was "fantastic". I will be making this again, but I will use some sort of whole-grain bread to add fiber and cut calories.

text:
Delicious!!!  We made this while it was still too cool out to grill so we spread the veggies out on a cookie sheet and baked them at 350 for about 15 minutes and then slid the bread in (with the mayo and feta on it) and cranked it up to broil for the last 10 or so minutes.  The veggies were perfectly tender and slightly golden and the cheese was soft and the bread toasty.   We used a hearty cracked wheat bread (heidelberg brand) and it was perfect!  I also replaced the fresh garlic with the jarred variety and used extra yellow squash because we didn't have any zucchini.  Finally, we replaced the red pepper with a green one and it was just as tasty!!  Highly recommended - a great way to spice up your veggies!

This was awesome!  I made it a little different though.
I used Tomato/Basil Foccacia--which was great!
I grilled zucchini and squash, portobello mushrooms and red onions on the George Foreman.  I had sauteed the mushrooms in Balsamic Vinaigrette dressing first.
I put Feta Cheese on the bread and under the broiler for a few minutes.
After the cheese melted a little bit, I added the above cooked veggies along with fresh spinach and sliced tomato!  I did use the mayo/garlic/lemon juice mix and it was seriously awesome
